< Review>
I am so grateful to G&M Towing & Recovery in Hesperia, CA! My son was volunteering about 20 miles from G&M Towing. He went to get large tanks of water refilled for the camp and the weight of it apparently made the car he was driving dig into the sandy shoulder dirt road and he was stuck in a hole. We couldn't find any other company to either answer their phone (and a few advertised 24 hour) or really want to rescue him with a winch without knowing his exact location which was difficult as the road turned into a dirt road to a camp. 2 other volunteers left the car and one got lost in the heat of the day!! My son stayed with the car along with another lady who had health issues that would be exacerbated. I thought I had found someone to get the car back on the road when I called Visa Roadside Dispatch but after waiting for hours and never getting the text I was told I would get and calling back several times.. ...they were not able to find a tow truck either. < review>
A while back, we decided to try Goodfellas Pizza.  It wasn't very good.  Thick chewy mushroom stems and a soggy crust.  I placed a review on Yelp accordingly.  Someone from Goodfellas wrote me a private message agreeing that the pizzas were not coming out well that night and he would like to make it up to me by giving me a complimentary pizza.

I responded that I would give it a try but he never responded back - empty promise.  I therefore allowed my review to stand.  This review is an edited version of the original.

At least year went by and we were craving pizza, Goodfellas was the only one open and we thought, hey, let's give them one more shot.  (There are sadly so few good choices here in Pacifica.)  We had them deliver a pizza with pesto, mushroom and artichoke hearts - NO RED SAUCE.  What we got was a pizza with red sauce and no pesto, plus the other ingredients.  I called them and explained what I had received and a female manager came to the phone and said she would send out another pizza that was correct.  I told her the last one had taken nearly an hour, it was late and we would prefer to have them make it up to us another way.  The manager told me that when I order next, the pizza would be complimentary to make up for the mistaken pizza.  I even asked her how that would happen and she stated that she would put a notation in my account accessible through my telephone number.  I thanked her.

Last night, I called Goodfellas to order that pizza.  I was told all they could do is knock off 10%.  Really?  I explained what had been promised based upon what had happened last time and a manager was brought to the phone.  She told me that all she was authorized to do is take 10% off otherwise she would have to call the owner/manager.  After a few minutes, a man called and identified himself as the owner.  He began by scolding me for using Yelp as a way to threaten and how do I think he feels hearing this, etc.  I told him I thought his customer service skills were lacking.  I reiterated my history (read above) with the business, essentially being owed at least one pizza but reminding him that my first experience with them was also a failure and a pizza was promised then, and then ignored after I accepted.  I pointed out that on two separate occasion, Goodfellas had sold me either a bad pizza (acknowledged by him) or a completely wrong pizza, and in both circumstances, promises of a complimentary pizza were made and later denied.

At the end of the phone conversation, the owner told me he doesn't feel like honoring those promises.  I used a "naughty" phrase and hung up the phone.

Bad, bad business.  Poor customer service and dishonest policies.  Never again Goodfellas!  I'd rather order an excellent pizza and have Waiters on Wheels deliver it.</review>

<Rate>5<//Rate><Text>As a Scotsman who likes good Indian style food. After two weeks of traveling around California it was a delight to see such a restaurant and even better to sample the delights of the food. The variety of the menu was excellent with all the usual foods you would expect and some extras as well. The service was very friendly and efficient, considering they were also hosting a wedding banquet in a separate area. The portions were large enough for two average eaters and the value for money was very good as well. The waiters advice was accurate and he was accommodating to our questions and needs.  The quality of the food was very good, with Pakora of both meat and veg, the Rita and spicy sauce where very flavoursome. The main meal had bags of favour and the rice fluffy as it should be, the breads were hot and tasty.  This meal goes down as the best meal of the holiday by all four of us. <userid>114482335506583349725<//userid><user_name>Shelly Highsmith< /user_name><date>1553122667485<//date>< Rating>
1</Rating>
<text>I have two little dogs that are brothers.  My vet closed approx. 6 years ago and I have been going to Animal Hospital of Thousand Oaks since..They have been pretty healthly so really the only time I have taken them in was for small things..nails cut, anal glands, etc. things like that..Our little Baxter just got so excited when he got to go to the "doctors" ..they were always real nice (expensive) to the dogs..This past Wednesday our little Baxter was breathing heavier then normal..so I called and Dr. Bass saw him..After doing blood work and x-ray she told me that I had caught it right away but he had chf (congestive heart failure) however she felt he would be fine after taking some Lasix to release the fluid..So I left feeling so good..I gave him his meds that she gave him, but the next day he seemed to be worse..I called Dr Bass and she talked to me right away..(this was on Friday) she adjusted his meds..I asked her if he got worse what would I do because she was not in until Monday again..She told me that the office was open till 1:00 on Saturday and if I needed them to call..Well, my poor sweet baby by morning was really laboring to breathe..I called the office around 10:00, I told the recepitionist what was going on..I told her that Dr. Bass had told me to call and come in..She said ok and I held on the phone until she talked to Dr Milburn, she came back to tell me that Dr. Milburn said to go to the emergency clinic..I said no..Baxter just had all his tests there..Dr. Bass told me to call..he needs a Lasix shot..she repeated again "Well, I can only tell you that Dr. Milburn is too busy with an emergency on a dog and wants you to go to the clinic..I told her I understood but he needs a lasix shot..I asked what time will she be available?  She had me hold and came back with a very nasty "Well, if you want to bring him in she will only give him a lasix shot"  Dr. Milburn could have cared less..I said you are open till 1:00 then the recepitionist said no we are closing today at 12:00..
I called my daughter in tears..she called her vet that hadn't seen little Baxter..it was Agoura Animal Clinic they had me bring him in ,  by the time I got there he was breathing even harder the Vet put him on oxygen..and how loving he was to my little guy..right away he said he didn't think it was from the CHF he wanted to take a 3 D xray..(they had called Animal Hospital of Thousand Oaks to get Baxters chart)(they had to call for the third time because the receptionist said he was not a patient) but funny after the third call from me and Agoura they finally found the chart and sent it..The vet took a 3 D xray and found that "Little Baxter" had a large mass in his liver and it was probably cancerous..with his breathing they could do nothing..I didn't want to put our little 8 ib. Baxter through that and felt I needed to let him go for him..
I tell this because I have raved about Animal Hospital of Thousand Oaks..however, it was never something critcal that was needed, this was the first time one of my "babies" needed real help..I don't blame Dr. Bass I like her as a vet and if she would have been on I feel she would have tried to help Baxter..but Dr. Milburn has in my opinion zero empathy when one of their patients are in trouble..She showed her true colors.
Also, got a sympathy card in the mail today.."It was from Agoura Animal Clinic where Little Baxter was put to rest..
Shame on Animal Hospital of Thousand Oaks..</text><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< resp>
None</resp>

<Time>1597697471602<//Time><Rating>5< /Rating><Review>Justin is a premium winery with excellent tasting options and food which will match any high end restaurant.

Located in the middle of the Paso Robles vineyards, it‚Äôs an excellent scenic drive to their establishment. When you arrive, you drive on loose gravel and are greeted by a welcoming staff.

Besides the excellent wine, the staff here are exceptional and very geared towards making your stay that much more enjoyable. You‚Äôre treated like royalty.

The seating area is booked right up against the vineyards which makes for a wonderful viewing. When tasting wine, it gives you a great sensation of tasting what you can see and makes you imagine the process of turning the grapes into the succulent nectar of wine, From farm to wine glass.

Price wise it is expensive, but they offer an excellent deal where for ever $100 you spend on wine bottles to go, the tasting fee ($35-$55) is completely waived. This made for an excellent tasting experience and if you plan on getting bottles to go, makes it a no brainer to do the bottles to go.

This is my personal favorite winery of all time and over the years, each wine has failed to disappoint. Their blends make for an exceptional tasting experience where taste buds are taken on a journey from a light hearted rose to a full bodied blend which takes you to euphoria.

Definitely a must for Paso Robles and is always on my list anytime I find myself in the area.<//Review>< Pics>

<userid>100902216978023131727<//userid><username>Michele Glemser<//username><Date>1494724672629<//Date><Rating>3</Rating><review>The wine is excellent.
The tasting facility is very beautiful and new, you are enveloped by the allure of wine and vineyard.
Our hostess Krystal was as sweet and down to earth as she could be and made us feel very comfortable.
The wine was absolutely lovely.
We tasted out on the "upper patio" and quickly learned that no tasting was allowed on the lower patio in the sun (it was chilly outside), that was our first indication of "not friendly".
Finished our tasting, my friend went into the tasting room/gift shop to use the restroom. I stayed outside for a few moments and followed there after.
As soon as I entered the tasting room a man approached me, and curtly asked if he could help me.
Honestly, I felt like I was trespasser in the way he addressed me!
(I am 63 years old, well dressed, and unassuming)
Good lawd...and then approached by another man in almost the same fashion. Really took me by surprise...these people need to chill.
That being said, the tasting atmosphere at Justin is very snooty and almost paranoid.
If you can get past that, the wine is fabulous.< /review><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMQ6EFa1egQXEtjjzWNE__S9J-ffrs8Tr43oJiB=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//pics>< response>

< text>
Love the view here, and it's always full of people from LA and the Bay. It's nestled in a beautiful valley outside Paso Robles, and the drive there is a thrill for those who enjoy winding curvy roads with blind curves and blind hills. There are moments when you literally creat a hill and you don't know if the road will curve to the right or left or if there'll be a drop of several feet. Beautiful road. The winery itself has great ambience, and is family friendly to a degree. Their outdoor seating is comfortable and tables are far apart from each other to afford some privacy and ensures nobody feels bothered by another group. Truly lovely corner of California here.</text>

I love Justin Wines and was really excited to make the pilgrimage to the vineyard.  My girlfriend and I arrived early for a tasting and found the tasting room sterile, boring, and lacking of character and vibe. < review>
If there was a way to give no stars for my recent experience at Justin Winery I would.  I decided to take my entire office staff on a wine tasting trip for their Christmas Party.  I had never been to Justin Winery, so this winery was the one that I was most excited to visit.  When we arrived, luckily, it was not very busy.  There were maybe 5 tables outside and 5 people inside the winery tasting room.  We sat down and waited to be greeted.  When our wine representative came over to the table, Gregory, he was less than friendly.  He did not smile, nor did he try and talk with us to see why we were there, the reason for the visit, etc.  He also did not explain the wines that we would be tasting.  We got our first pour of wine after about 10 to 15 minutes of waiting.  During this time, one of my staff members told Gregory that one of his family members wanted to join the wine club.  Of course, he immediately started working on that on the phone inside.  After we waited and waited for our second pour of wine, one of my employees finally had to go into the actual building and ask for a second pour from another wine representative.  When, Gregory finally finished his phone call and came out with the second pour of wine, he made a comment about my staff member that went into the building to ask for our second pour.  After rolling his eyes, he stated, "Well if she would just quit hounding me" I would come out here and pour wine.  This was the first time anyone had went inside the building.  Gregory was unprofessional, extremely rude, and an outright negative individual.  I have no idea how he would even be able to obtain a job such as this.  Because of my experience with Gregory, I may never go back to Justin.  It is too bad because the wine is very nice!</review>

< text>
Their tasting menu is very good, and they frequently offer samples of their higher end reserve wines.  Their Cab is very good, the reserve cab is fantastic.  Some of the wines available are difficult to find, or unavailable, at other retail outlets.  The place is very corporate, but that is not bad too me. The tasting room is beautiful and modern. The staff is very friendly, and the restaurant and atmosphere...dare I say it...is worth the price.  Some of the comments here make me think that they were at a different winery, or that they were the reason behind the bad experience. You can find better wines in the area, but probably not a single vineyard with as many high quality wines.<//text>

<username>Steff A.< /username><Time>1565390630768</Time><rate>4</rate><text>The BFF is such a fan of Justin Vineyard and after our tasting experience, I get it now.  Party of 13 please....

We stopped in on a hot Saturday afternoon and Larry was our tasting guide.   He was friendly, professional and we learned plenty about the wines we sampled as well as the Justin Vineyard and history.  We had rookies and seasoned Wine veterans and Justin worked well with both.
Our tasting included:
2016 Viognier - Light, refreshingly perfect for the hot day.
2016 Reserve Cabernet Sauvignon - Best Cabernet I've tasted this year.
2016 Reserve Tempranillo - Dark, deep, tasty.
2016 Reserve Malbec - Love Malbecs and this might be my new fav.  I purchased two bottles as souvenirs
2015 Isoceles Reserve - Award winner, lovely and I'll be stashing a bottle at home.

The lobby and showroom is spacious and organized well.  They have plenty of Justin items that covers souvenirs, apparel, to wine accessories of course.  You can also pick up some snacks, cheese, crackers to add to your tasting experience.

In the patio there's some great patio seating with great view of this lovely property with the vines and the mountains in the distance.  There are definitely plenty of social media moments here.  If in the area, Justin is a definite visit to enjoy some great wine and make even greater memories.  Cheers!</text>< Pictures>

< GmapID>
0x80ed29f7f823a82d:0xb550b7414f39c66d</GmapID>
</record>
</dataset><record>
<pics>None</pics>< Text>
JUSTIN Vineyards and Winery is a beautiful place to stop for wine tasting, lunch, and a winery tour. The tasting room and restaurant stands out like a contemporary ranch house amongst the surrounding vineyards. Row upon row of vines stretch across the land and hills like fine stitch work. If you decide to stay for lunch, here are a few suggestions from the menu:

A great way to try the wines while enjoying a meal is with a flight. The White Wine Flight includes 2014 JUSTIN Sauvignon Blanc, 2014 JUSTIN Ros√©, and 2013 Landmark Overlook Chardonnay. The Sauvignon Blanc has a pear nose. Green apple and peach flavors are experienced on the palate with a light, clean finish. Rating: 3.5/5. The Ros√© has a blackberry and cherry aroma. Strawberry and grapefruit flavors are experienced on the palate with a nice, clean finish. Rating: 4.5/5. The Chardonnay has a white grape and pear aroma. White grape, pear, floral, and mineral flavors experienced on the palate. Rating: 2.5/5

Windrose Farm Lamb Tartare is topped with garden greens, preserved lemon aioli, and crostini. This was a fantastic take on tartare. The lamb was sweet and minced perfectly. The use of shaved egg yolk added a richness to the dish without the mess of a runny egg yolk. The fresh greens from the garden paired nicely. Rating: 4.5/5

JUSTIN Fries are tossed with truffle salt, parmesan, and JUSTIN fine herb blend. The fries were light and crispy. The truffle flavor was just right so the parmesan and herbs could shine as well. Rating: 4.5/5

Bucatini Pasta tossed with Alle-Pia sausage, wild mushrooms, bitter greens, smoked butter, and parmesan. This was an excellence lunch dish, light yet satisfying. The sauce had a rich creamy texture. The flavors of the succulent mushrooms and lean, meaty sausage balanced perfectly with the sauce and pasta. Rating: 4.5/5

JUSTIN Brownies topped with caramel, cocoa nibs, and served with lemon balm ice cream. The brownie was served warm with rich, decadent chocolate flavor. Caramel sauce made the dish more luxurious. The lemon balm ice cream was refreshing with unexpected herbal notes. It was different and made a nice contrast to the brownie. Rating: 3.8/5

After lunch, a walking tour is a great way to burn some calories. JUSTIN Vineyards and Winery offers tours of their facility. Be sure to call ahead for a reservation as the tours are limited to 10 people per tour. Our tour guide, Larry, took us around the winery, showing us the machinery used to mill and press the grapes during harvest and the large stainless steel tanks used for the fermentation process. He then walked us through the caves where the different wines are aged in French Oak barrels. You will also be tasting wine along the way - Ros√©, Merlot, Petit Syrah, and Reserve. You'll also notice that scattered around the vineyard are poles with metal boxes on top. They sort of look like large bird houses. They are homes for the owls who rid the vineyards of rodents and snakes. They let nature take on the job of pest control so chemical pesticides are not used.

After the tour, head back to the tasting room to sample and purchase your favorite wines. Take a walk around the on-site vegetable garden where they grow the produce that is ultimately going to end up on your plate in the restaurant - kale, different varieties of lettuce, edible flowers, Swiss chard, and more. Lady bugs and praying mantis are also natural pest controllers and are on patrol here as well.<//Text>
